			<div class="after-portlet after-portlet-lang"><span class="wb-langlinks-edit wb-langlinks-link"><a href="https://www.wikidata.org/wiki/Special:EntityPage/Q35878#sitelinks-wikipedia" title="Edit interlanguage links" class="wbc-editpage">Edit links</a></span></div>
		</div>

	</div>
</div>
</header>

					<div id="mw-content-text" class="mw-body-content"><div class="mw-content-ltr mw-parser-output" lang="en" dir="ltr"><div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">Language isolate of New Mexico, United States</div>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1033289096">.mw-parser-output .hatnote{font-style:italic}.mw-parser-output div.hatnote{padding-left:1.6em;margin-bottom:0.5em}.mw-parser-output .hatnote i{font-style:normal}.mw-parser-output .hatnote+link+.hatnote{margin-top:-0.5em}</style><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">"Keresan" redirects here. For the US Navy cargo ship, see <a href="/wiki/USS_Keresan_(ID-1806)" class="mw-redirect" title="USS Keresan (ID-1806)">USS Keresan (ID-1806)</a>.</div>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1126788409">.mw-parser-output .plainlist ol,.mw-parser-output .plainlist ul{line-height:inherit;list-style:none;margin:0;padding:0}.mw-parser-output .plainlist ol li,.mw-parser-output .plainlist ul li{margin-bottom:0}</style><style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1066479718">.mw-parser-output .infobox-subbox{padding:0;border:none;margin:-3px;width:auto;min-width:100%;font-size:100%;clear:none;float:none;background-color:transparent}.mw-parser-output .infobox-3cols-child{margin:auto}.mw-parser-output .infobox .navbar{font-size:100%}body.skin-minerva .mw-parser-output .infobox-header,body.skin-minerva .mw-parser-output .infobox-subheader,body.skin-minerva .mw-parser-output .infobox-above,body.skin-minerva .mw-parser-output .infobox-title,body.skin-minerva .mw-parser-output .infobox-image,body.skin-minerva .mw-parser-output .infobox-full-data,body.skin-minerva .mw-parser-output .infobox-below{text-align:center}</style><table class="infobox vevent"><tbody><tr><th colspan="2" class="infobox-above above" style="font-size:125%; color: black; background-color:  #c0dde6;">Keresan</th></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label" style="white-space:nowrap;padding-right:0.65em;">Native&#160;to</th><td class="infobox-data" style="line-height:1.3em;">United States</td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label" style="white-space:nowrap;padding-right:0.65em;">Region</th><td class="infobox-data" style="line-height:1.3em;"><a href="/wiki/New_Mexico" title="New Mexico">New Mexico</a></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label" style="white-space:nowrap;padding-right:0.65em;">Ethnicity</th><td class="infobox-data" style="line-height:1.3em;"><a href="/wiki/Keres_people" title="Keres people">Keres</a></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label" style="white-space:nowrap;padding-right:0.65em;"><div style="display: inline-block; line-height: 1.2em; padding: .1em 0;">Native speakers</div></th><td class="infobox-data" style="line-height:1.3em;">13,190&#160;(2013)<sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label" style="white-space:nowrap;padding-right:0.65em;"><div style="display: inline-block; line-height: 1.2em; padding: .1em 0;"><span class="wrap"><a href="/wiki/Language_family" title="Language family">Language family</a></span></div></th><td class="infobox-data" style="line-height:1.3em;"><div style="text-align:left;"><a href="/wiki/Language_isolate" title="Language isolate">Language isolate</a></div></td></tr><tr class="plainlist"><th scope="row" class="infobox-label" style="white-space:nowrap;padding-right:0.65em;">Dialects</th><td class="infobox-data" style="line-height:1.3em;">
<ul><li>East Keres</li>
<li>West Keres</li></ul>
</td></tr><tr><th colspan="2" class="infobox-header" style="color: black; background-color:  #c0dde6;">Language codes</th></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label" style="white-space:nowrap;padding-right:0.65em;"><span class="nowrap"><a href="/wiki/ISO_639-3" title="ISO 639-3">ISO 639-3</a></span></th><td class="infobox-data" style="line-height:1.3em;">Either:<br /><code><a href="https://iso639-3.sil.org/code/kee" class="extiw" title="iso639-3:kee">kee</a></code>&#160;–&#160;Eastern<br /><code><a href="https://iso639-3.sil.org/code/kjq" class="extiw" title="iso639-3:kjq">kjq</a></code>&#160;–&#160;Western</td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label" style="white-space:nowrap;padding-right:0.65em;"><i><a href="/wiki/Glottolog" title="Glottolog">Glottolog</a></i></th><td class="infobox-data" style="line-height:1.3em;"><code><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://glottolog.org/resource/languoid/id/kere1287">kere1287</a></code></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label" style="white-space:nowrap;padding-right:0.65em;"><a href="/wiki/Endangered_Languages_Project" title="Endangered Languages Project">ELP</a></th><td class="infobox-data" style="line-height:1.3em;"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1126788409"><div class="plainlist"><ul><li><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.endangeredlanguages.com/lang/650">Acoma-Laguna</a></li><li><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.endangeredlanguages.com/lang/6511">Rio Grande Keresan</a></li></ul></div></td></tr><tr><td colspan="2" class="infobox-full-data" style="line-height:1.3em;"><span class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Frameless"><a href="/wiki/File:Keres_langs.png" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Keres_langs.png/320px-Keres_langs.png" decoding="async" width="320" height="311" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Keres_langs.png/480px-Keres_langs.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/2/22/Keres_langs.png 2x" data-file-width="615" data-file-height="597" /></a></span><div style="text-align:left;">Pre-contact distribution of Keresan languages</div></td></tr><tr><td colspan="2" class="infobox-full-data" style="line-height:1.3em;"><span class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Frameless"><a href="/wiki/File:Lang_Status_60-DE.svg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Lang_Status_60-DE.svg/320px-Lang_Status_60-DE.svg.png" decoding="async" width="320" height="96" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Lang_Status_60-DE.svg/480px-Lang_Status_60-DE.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Lang_Status_60-DE.svg/640px-Lang_Status_60-DE.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="153" /></a></span><div style="text-align:left;"><div class="center" style="width:auto; margin-left:auto; margin-right:auto;"><span style="font-size:85%;">Acoma-Laguna is classified as Definitely Endangered by the <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a> <a href="/wiki/Atlas_of_the_World%27s_Languages_in_Danger" title="Atlas of the World&#39;s Languages in Danger">Atlas of the World's Languages in Danger</a></span></div></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p><b>Keres</b> (<span class="rt-commentedText nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt" lang="en-fonipa"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="&#39;k&#39; in &#39;kind&#39;">k</span><span title="/ə/: &#39;a&#39; in &#39;about&#39;">ə</span><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="&#39;r&#39; in &#39;rye&#39;">r</span><span title="/iː/: &#39;ee&#39; in &#39;fleece&#39;">iː</span><span title="&#39;s&#39; in &#39;sigh&#39;">s</span></span>/</a></span></span>), also <b>Keresan</b> (<span class="rt-commentedText nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt" lang="en-fonipa"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="&#39;k&#39; in &#39;kind&#39;">k</span><span title="/ɛ/: &#39;e&#39; in &#39;dress&#39;">ɛ</span><span title="&#39;r&#39; in &#39;rye&#39;">r</span><span title="/ɪ/: &#39;i&#39; in &#39;kit&#39;">ɪ</span><span title="&#39;s&#39; in &#39;sigh&#39;">s</span><span title="/ən/: &#39;on&#39; in &#39;button&#39;">ən</span></span>/</a></span></span>), is a <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_languages_of_the_Americas" title="Indigenous languages of the Americas">Native American language</a>, spoken by the <a href="/wiki/Keres_people" title="Keres people">Keres</a> <a href="/wiki/Pueblo_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Pueblo people">Pueblo people</a> in <a href="/wiki/New_Mexico" title="New Mexico">New Mexico</a>. Depending on the analysis, Keres is considered a small <a href="/wiki/Language_family" title="Language family">language family</a> or a <a href="/wiki/Language_isolate" title="Language isolate">language isolate</a> with several <a href="/wiki/Dialect_cluster" class="mw-redirect" title="Dialect cluster">dialects</a>. The varieties of each of the seven Keres pueblos are <a href="/wiki/Mutually_intelligible" class="mw-redirect" title="Mutually intelligible">mutually intelligible</a> with its closest neighbors. There are significant differences between the Western and Eastern groups, which are sometimes counted as separate languages.
</p>
<meta property="mw:PageProp/toc" />
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Family_division">Family division</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Keres_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Family division"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>In 2007, there was an estimate total of 10,670 speakers.<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1116488514">.mw-parser-output .treeview ul{padding:0;margin:0}.mw-parser-output .treeview li{padding:0;margin:0;list-style-type:none;list-style-image:none}.mw-parser-output .treeview li li{background:url("https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/f/f2/Treeview-grey-line.png")no-repeat 0 -2981px;padding-left:21px;text-indent:0.3em}.mw-parser-output .treeview li li:last-child{background-position:0 -5971px}.mw-parser-output .treeview li.emptyline>ul>.mw-empty-elt:first-child+.emptyline,.mw-parser-output .treeview li.emptyline>ul>li:first-child{background-position:0 9px}</style><div class="treeview">
<ul><li><b>Keres</b>
<ul><li><b>Eastern Keres</b>: total of 4,580 speakers (1990 census)
<ul><li><b><a href="/wiki/Cochiti_Pueblo" class="mw-redirect" title="Cochiti Pueblo">Cochiti Pueblo</a></b> <i>Kotyit dialect</i>: 600 speakers (2007)</li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/San_Felipe_Pueblo" class="mw-redirect" title="San Felipe Pueblo">San Felipe Pueblo</a></b> <i>Katishtya dialect</i>: 2,340 speakers (2007)</li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Kewa_Pueblo" class="mw-redirect" title="Kewa Pueblo">Kewa Pueblo</a></b> (formally <b>Santo Domingo Pueblo</b>) <i>Kewa dialect</i>: 2,850 speakers (2007)</li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Zia_Pueblo" class="mw-redirect" title="Zia Pueblo">Zia Pueblo</a></b> <i>Ts'ia dialect</i>: 500 speakers (2007)</li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Santa_Ana_Pueblo" class="mw-redirect" title="Santa Ana Pueblo">Santa Ana Pueblo</a></b> <i>Tamaiya dialect</i>: 390 speakers (2007)</li></ul></li>
<li><b>Western Keres</b>: total of 3,391 speakers (1990 census)
<ul><li><b><a href="/wiki/Acoma_Pueblo" title="Acoma Pueblo">Acoma Pueblo</a></b>  <i>Áakʼu dialect</i>: 1,930 speakers (2007)</li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Laguna,_New_Mexico" title="Laguna, New Mexico">Laguna Pueblo</a></b> <i>Kawaika dialect</i>: 2,060 speakers (2007)</li></ul></li></ul></li></ul>
</div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Genetic_relationships">Genetic relationships</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Keres_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Genetic relationships"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Keres is now considered a <a href="/wiki/Language_isolate" title="Language isolate">language isolate</a>. In the past, <a href="/wiki/Edward_Sapir" title="Edward Sapir">Edward Sapir</a> grouped it together with a <a href="/wiki/Hokan_languages" title="Hokan languages">Hokan</a>–Siouan stock. <a href="/wiki/Morris_Swadesh" title="Morris Swadesh">Morris Swadesh</a> suggested a connection with <a href="/wiki/Wichita_language" title="Wichita language">Wichita</a>. <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Greenberg" title="Joseph Greenberg">Joseph Greenberg</a> grouped Keres with <a href="/wiki/Siouan" class="mw-redirect" title="Siouan">Siouan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Yuchi_language" title="Yuchi language">Yuchi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Caddoan" class="mw-redirect" title="Caddoan">Caddoan</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Iroquoian" class="mw-redirect" title="Iroquoian">Iroquoian</a> in a superstock called Keresiouan. None of these proposals has been validated by subsequent linguistic research.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Phonology">Phonology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Keres_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Phonology"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Keresan has between 42 and 45 consonant sounds, and around 40 vowel sounds, adding up to a total of about 85 <a href="/wiki/Phoneme" title="Phoneme">phonemes</a>, depending on the analysis and the language variety. Based on the classification in the <a href="/wiki/World_Atlas_of_Language_Structures" title="World Atlas of Language Structures">World Atlas of Language Structures</a>, Keres is a language with a <i>large</i> consonant inventory.
</p><p>The great number of consonants relates to the three-way distinction between <a href="/wiki/Voicelessness" title="Voicelessness">voiceless</a>, <a href="/wiki/Aspirated_consonant" title="Aspirated consonant">aspirated</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ejective_consonant" title="Ejective consonant">ejective</a> consonants (e.g. /t tʰ tʼ/), and to the larger than average<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> number of <a href="/wiki/Fricative_consonant" class="mw-redirect" title="Fricative consonant">fricatives</a> (i.e. /s sʼ ʂ ʂʼ ʃ ʃʼ h/) and <a href="/wiki/Affricate_consonant" class="mw-redirect" title="Affricate consonant">affricates</a>, the latter also showing the three-way distinction found in <a href="/wiki/Stop_consonant" class="mw-redirect" title="Stop consonant">stops</a>.
</p><p>The large number of vowels derives from a distinction made between <a href="/wiki/Vowel_length" title="Vowel length">long</a> and short vowels (e.g. /e eː/), as well as from the presence of <a href="/wiki/Tone_(linguistics)" title="Tone (linguistics)">tones</a> and voicelessness. Thus, a single vowel quality may occur with seven distinct realizations: /é è e̥ éː èː êː ěː/, all of which are used to distinguish words in the language.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Consonants">Consonants</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Keres_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Consonants"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

Miller">Miller</a> &amp; Davis (1963) based on a comparison of Acoma, Santa Ana, and Santo Domingo, as well as other features of the dialects compiled from <i>The Language of Santa Ana Pueblo</i> (1964), <i>Kansas Working Papers in Linguistics</i> (1987), and <i>The Phonemes of Keresan</i> (1946), and the <i>Grammar of Laguna Keres</i> (2005).<sup id="cite_ref-:0_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:2_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:1_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:4_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:4-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Vowels">Vowels</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Keres_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Vowels"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Keresan vowels have a <a href="/wiki/Phoneme" title="Phoneme">phonemic</a> distinction in <a href="/wiki/Vowel_length" title="Vowel length">duration</a>: all vowels can be long or short. Additionally, short vowels can also be voiceless. The vowel chart below contains the vowel phonemes and allophones from the information of the Keresan languages combined from <i>The Language of Santa Ana Pueblo</i> (1964),<sup id="cite_ref-:0_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> <i>The Phonemes of Keresan</i> (1946),<sup id="cite_ref-:1_6-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> and Kansas Working Papers in Linguistics (1987).<sup id="cite_ref-:2_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<p>Notes:
</p>
<ul><li>Western Keres does not have phonemic /oː/ or /o/, though both vowels may occur phonetically.<sup id="cite_ref-:4_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:4-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> Eastern Keres words containing /o/ show /au/ in Western Keres.<sup id="cite_ref-:5_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:5-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> For instance, the first vowel in the word-sentence <i>Sraúka̠cha̠</i> – “I see you”:
<ul><li>Kotyit Keres: [ʂóːkʰɑ̥tʃʰɑ̥]</li>
<li>Kʼawaika Keres: [ʂɑ̌ukʰɑ̥tʃʰɑ̥]</li></ul></li></ul>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Voiceless_vowels">Voiceless vowels</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Keres_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Voiceless vowels"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>All Keresan short vowels may be <a href="/wiki/Voicelessness" title="Voicelessness">devoiced</a> in certain positions. The phonemic status of these vowels is controversial.<sup id="cite_ref-:4_7-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:4-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> Maring (1967) considers them to be phonemes of Áákʼu Keres, whereas other authors disagree. There are phonetic grounds for vowel devoicing based on the environment they occur, for instance word-finally, but there are also exceptions. Vowels in final position are nearly always voiceless and medial vowels occurring between voiced consonants, after nasals and ejectives are nearly always voiced.<sup id="cite_ref-:3_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:3-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<ul><li>Word-final devoicing: [pɑ̌ːkʊ̥] <i>because</i></li>
<li>Word-medial devoicing: [ʔìpʰi̥ʃɑ́] <i>white paint</i></li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tones">Tones</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Keres_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Tones"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Acoma Keres has four <a href="/wiki/Tone_(linguistics)" title="Tone (linguistics)">lexical tones</a>: high, low, falling and rising.<sup id="cite_ref-:3_9-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:3-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> Falling and rising tones only occur in long vowels and voiceless vowels bear no tones:
</p>
<table class="wikitable">

<tbody><tr>
<th><i>Tones</i>
</th>
<th>examples
</th>
<th>translation
</th></tr>
<tr style="text-align:center;">
<th>High
</th>
<td>[tɨ́j], [áwáʔáwá]
</td>
<td><i>here, matrilineal uncle</i>
</td></tr>
<tr style="text-align:center;">
<th>Low
</th>
<td>[mùːtètsá]
</td>
<td><i>young boy</i>
</td></tr>
<tr style="text-align:center;">
<th>Rising
</th>
<td>[pɑ̌ːkʊ̥]
</td>
<td><i>because</i>
</td></tr>
<tr style="text-align:center;">
<th>Falling
</th>
<td>[ʔêː], [hêːk'a]
</td>
<td><i>and, whole part</i>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Syllable_structure">Syllable structure</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Keres_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Syllable structure"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Most Keresan syllables take a CV(V) shape.<sup id="cite_ref-:4_7-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:4-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> The maximal syllable structure is CCVVC and the minimal syllable is CV. In native Keresan words, only a glottal stop /ʔ/ ⟨ʼ⟩ can close a syllable, but some loanwords from Spanish have syllables that end in a consonant, mostly a nasal (i.e. /m n/ but words containing these sequences are rare in the language.<sup id="cite_ref-:6_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:6-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<table class="wikitable">

<tbody><tr>
<th><i>Syllable type</i>
</th>
<th>examples
</th>
<th>translation
</th></tr>
<tr style="text-align:center;">
<th>CV
</th>
<td>[sʼà], [ʔɪ]shv́v
</td>
<td><i>I have it, left</i>
</td></tr>
<tr style="text-align:center;">
<th>CVV
</th>
<td>[mùː]dedza, a[táù]shi
</td>
<td><i>young boy</i>, <i>cooking pot</i>
</td></tr>
<tr style="text-align:center;">
<th>CCV
</th>
<td>[ʃkʰí]srátsʼa
</td>
<td><i>I'm not fat</i>
</td></tr>
<tr style="text-align:center;">
<th>CCVV
</th>
<td>[ʃtùː]sra
</td>
<td><i>bluejay</i>
</td></tr>
<tr style="text-align:center;">
<th>CVC
</th>
<td>í[miʔ], [kùm]banêeru
</td>
<td><i>expression of fear, workmate</i> (Spanish <i>"compañero"</i>)
</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>Due to extensive vowel devoicing, several Keresan words may be perceived as ending in consonants or even containing consonant clusters.
</p>
<ul><li>Word-internal cluster: <i>yʼâakạ srûunị</i> ‘stomach’ /jˀɑ̂ːkḁʂûːni/ &gt; [jɑ̂ːkḁʂûːni] ~ [jɑ̂ː<b>kʂ</b>ûːni]</li>
<li>Word-final coda: <i>úwàakạ</i> ‘baby’; /úwɑ̀ːkḁ/ &gt; [úwɑ̀ːkʰḁ] ~ [úwɑ̀ː<b>kʰ</b>]</li></ul>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Phonotactics">Phonotactics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Keres_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Phonotactics"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The only sequence of consonants (i.e. <a href="/wiki/Consonant_cluster" title="Consonant cluster">consonant cluster</a>) that occurs in native Keresan words is a sequence of a fricative /ʃ ʂ/ and a stop or affricate. Clusters are restricted to beginnings of syllables (i.e. the <a href="/wiki/Syllable" title="Syllable">syllable onset</a>). When the alveolo-palatal consonant /ʃ/ occurs as C<sub>1</sub>, it combines with alveolar and palatal C<sub>2</sub>, whereas the retroflex alveolar /ʂ/ precedes bilabial and velar C<sub>2</sub>s, which suggest a complementary distribution. Consonant clusters may occur both word-initially and word-medially.<sup id="cite_ref-:5_8-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:5-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Orthography">Orthography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Keres_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Orthography"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Traditional Keresan beliefs postulate that Keres is a sacred language that must exist only in its spoken form.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> The language's religious connotation and years of persecution of Pueblo religion by European colonizers may also explain why no unified orthographic convention exists for Keresan. However, a practical spelling system has been developed for Laguna (Kʼawaika)<sup id="cite_ref-:4_7-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:4-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> and more recently for Acoma (Áakʼu) Keres,<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> both of which are remarkably consistent.
</p><p>In the Keres spelling system, each symbol represents a single phoneme. The letters ⟨c q z f⟩ and sometimes also ⟨v⟩ are not used. <a href="/wiki/Digraph_(orthography)" title="Digraph (orthography)">Digraphs</a> represent both palatal consonants (written using a sequence of C and ⟨y⟩), and retroflex consonants, which are represented using a sequence of C and the letter ⟨r⟩. These <a href="/wiki/Graphemes" class="mw-redirect" title="Graphemes">graphemes</a> used for writing Western Keres are shown between ⟨...⟩ below.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Consonant_symbols">Consonant symbols</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Keres_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Consonant symbols"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Vowel_symbols">Vowel symbols</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Keres_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Vowel symbols"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Vowel sounds are represented straightforwardly in the existing spellings for Keresan. Each vowel sound is written using a unique letter or digraph (for long vowels and <a href="/wiki/Diphthongs" class="mw-redirect" title="Diphthongs">diphthongs</a>). However, there are two competing representations for the vowel /ɨ/. Some versions simply use the <a href="/wiki/International_Phonetic_Alphabet" title="International Phonetic Alphabet">IPA</a> ⟨ɨ⟩ whereas others use the letter ⟨v⟩ (the sound /v/ as in <i>veal</i> does not occur in Keresan). Voiceless vowels have also been represented in two ways; either underlined or with a dot below (see table).
</p>

<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Diacritics_for_tone">Diacritics for tone</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Keres_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Diacritics for tone"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Tone may or may not be represented in the orthography of Keresan. When represented, four diacritics may be used above the vowel. Unlike the system used for <a href="/wiki/Navajo_language" title="Navajo language">Navajo</a>, diacritics for tone are not repeated in long vowels. 
</p>
<table class="wikitable">

<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Keres_alphabet_and_alphabetical_order">Keres alphabet and alphabetical order</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Keres_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Keres alphabet and alphabetical order"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Although Keresan is not normally written, there exists only one dictionary of the language in which words are listed in any given order. In this <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://dictionary.keres.co/">dictionary</a> of Western Keres, digraphs count as single letters, although ejective consonants are not listed separately; occurring after their non-ejective counterparts. The glottal stop ⟨ʼ⟩  and long vowels (e.g. ⟨aa ee ii⟩ etc.) are not treated as separate letters.
</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sample_texts">Sample texts</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Keres_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Sample texts"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Orthography_marking_tone">Orthography marking tone</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Keres_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Orthography marking tone"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<dl><dt>Woodpecker and Coyote<sup id="cite_ref-:5_8-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:5-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup></dt></dl>
<dl><dd>⟨Ái dítʼîishu srbígà kʼánâaya dyáʼâʼu. Shʼée srbígà ái dyěitsị ái náyáa shdyɨ dyáʼa.⟩</dd>
<dd>/ ɑ́ì títʼîːʃù ʂpíkɑ̀ kʼɑ́nɑ̂ːjɑ̀ cɑ́ʔɑ̂ʔù | ʃʼéː ʂpíkɑ̀ ɑ́ì cěǐtsʰi̥ ɑ́ì nɑ́jɑ́ː ʃcɨ̀ cɑ́ʔɑ̀ /</dd></dl>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Orthography_without_tone_marking">Orthography without tone marking</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Keres_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Orthography without tone marking"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<dl><dt>Boas text<sup id="cite_ref-:4_7-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:4-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup></dt></dl>
<dl><dd>Baanaʼa, egu kauʼseeʼe, atsi sʼaama-ee srayutse.</dd></dl>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Morphosyntax">Morphosyntax</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Keres_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Morphosyntax"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Keresan is a <a href="/wiki/Split_ergativity" title="Split ergativity">split-ergative</a> language in which verbs denoting states (i.e. <a href="/wiki/Stative_verb" title="Stative verb">stative verbs</a>) behave differently from those indexing actions, especially in terms of the <a href="/wiki/Grammatical_person" title="Grammatical person">person</a> <a href="/wiki/Affix" title="Affix">affixes</a> they take. This system of <a href="/wiki/Argument_(linguistics)" title="Argument (linguistics)">argument</a> marking is based on a split-intransitive pattern, in which <a href="/wiki/Subject_(grammar)" title="Subject (grammar)">subjects</a> are marked differently if they are perceived as actors than from when they are perceived as undergoers of the action being described.
</p><p>The morphology of Keresan is mostly <a href="/wiki/Prefix" title="Prefix">prefixing</a>, although <a href="/wiki/Suffix" title="Suffix">suffixes</a> and <a href="/wiki/Reduplication" title="Reduplication">reduplication</a> also occur.<sup id="cite_ref-:5_8-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:5-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> Keresan distinguishes <a href="/wiki/Noun" title="Noun">nouns</a>, verbs, <a href="/wiki/Numeral_(linguistics)" title="Numeral (linguistics)">numerals</a> and <a href="/wiki/Grammatical_particle" title="Grammatical particle">particles</a> as word classes. Nouns in Keresan do not normally distinguish <a href="/wiki/Grammatical_case" title="Grammatical case">case</a> or <a href="/wiki/Grammatical_number" title="Grammatical number">number</a>, but they can be <a href="/wiki/Agreement_(linguistics)" title="Agreement (linguistics)">inflected</a> for <a href="/wiki/Grammatical_possession" class="mw-redirect" title="Grammatical possession">possession</a>, with distinct constructions for <a href="/wiki/Inalienable_possession" title="Inalienable possession">alienable</a> and inalienable possession. Other than possession, Keresan nouns show no comprehensive <a href="/wiki/Noun_class" title="Noun class">noun classes</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Word_order">Word order</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Keres_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Word order"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Keresan is a <a href="/wiki/Word_order" title="Word order">verb-final</a> language, though word order is rather flexible.<sup id="cite_ref-:5_8-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:5-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:4_7-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:4-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="interlinear" style="margin-left:2em"><div>Laguna Keres:<sup id="cite_ref-:4_7-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:4-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">John</p><p style="margin: 0px;">J.</p><p style="margin: 0px;">John</p><p style="margin: 0px;font-variant: small-caps;">subject</p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">Bill</p><p style="margin: 0px;">B.</p><p style="margin: 0px;">Bill</p><p style="margin: 0px;font-variant: small-caps;">object</p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">gukacha</p><p style="margin: 0px;">g-Ø-ukacha</p><p style="margin: 0px;"><abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="third person, singular" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">3S</abbr>-<abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="third person, singular" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">3S</abbr>-see</p><p style="margin: 0px;font-variant: small-caps;">verb</p></div><p style="display: none;">John Bill gukacha</p><p style="display: none;">J. B. g-Ø-ukacha</p><p style="display: none;">John Bill 3S-3S-see</p><p style="display: none;">subject object verb</p><p style="clear: left;">'John saw Bill.'</p><div style="clear: left; display: block;"></div>
</div>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Negation">Negation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Keres_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Negation"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Negation is doubly marked in Keresan. In addition to the adverb <i>dzaadi</i>, verbs index negation through a suffix (e.g. <i>-u</i>).
</p>
<ul><li><i>Gukacha</i> 'S/he saw her/him'</li>
<li><i><b>Dzaadi</b> gukacha<b>u</b></i> 'S/he didn't see her/him'</li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Verbal_morphology">Verbal morphology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Keres_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Verbal morphology"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Verb" title="Verb">verb</a> is a central <a href="/wiki/Grammatical_category" title="Grammatical category">grammatical category</a> in Keres, conveying the most information about events in communicative acts.<sup id="cite_ref-:4_7-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:4-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:5_8-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:5-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:3_9-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:3-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> Through its <a href="/wiki/Morpheme" title="Morpheme">morphemes</a>, Keresan verbs code not only person and number of the initiator of the action (e.g. “Tammy drink<b>s</b> decaf”) as is common in <a href="/wiki/Indo-European_languages" title="Indo-European languages">Indo-European languages</a>, but also how the initiator is implicated in the action. For instance, the three verbs that describe Tammy's actions in “Tammy kicked the ball” vs. “Tammy jumped” vs. “Tammy sneezed” require different levels of effort from Tammy, that is when <i>kicking</i> vs. <i>jumping</i> vs. <i>sneezing</i>.
</p><p>Additionally, the person and number of the undergoer of the action are all coded on the verb (e.g. the word <i>gukacha</i> means “S/he sees her/him”, a full sentence in English). The ways the speaker assesses the action (i.e. <a href="/wiki/Evidentiality" title="Evidentiality">evidentiality</a>, as in “I think Tammy arrived from class” vs. “Tammy arrived from class”). Finally, the internal temporal structure of the action (i.e. <a href="/wiki/Aspect_(grammar)" class="mw-redirect" title="Aspect (grammar)">aspect</a>, as in “Tammy <b>was</b> sneez<b>ing</b> in class” vs. “Tammy sneez<b>ed</b> in class”) is also coded in Keresan verbs.
</p><p>According to Maring (1967), the Keresan verb is organized around the following grammatical categories (pp.&#160;39–40)<sup id="cite_ref-:3_9-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:3-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<ul><li><i><b>Subject/Object relations</b></i>
<ul><li><i>Subject of intransitive verbs:</i> marked by a prefix that distinguishes 3-4 persons in the singular (see below).</li>
<li><i>Subject of transitive verbs:</i> marked by a prefix that distinguishes 3-4 persons in the singular (see below).</li>
<li><i>Object of transitive verbs:</i> marked by a prefix that combines with the subject prefix, or by a <a href="/wiki/Suffix" title="Suffix">suffix</a></li></ul></li>
<li><i><b>Number relations</b></i>
<ul><li><i>Singular:</i> usually marked by a prefix</li>
<li><i>Dual:</i> can be marked by a prefix, partial reduplication or by suffixes</li>
<li><i>Plural:</i> can be marked by a prefix, partial reduplication, by suffixes or by <a href="/wiki/Suppletion" title="Suppletion">suppletive stem forms</a> (i.e. singular and plural forms are not related <a href="/wiki/Etymology" title="Etymology">etymologically</a>)</li></ul></li>
<li><i><b>Temporal relations</b></i>
<ul><li><i>Future:</i> is marked on the verb by a series of prefixes that also encode number</li></ul></li>
<li><i><b>Modality relations</b></i>
<ul><li><i>Indicative</i></li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Dubitative" class="mw-redirect" title="Dubitative">Dubitative</a></i></li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Hortative" title="Hortative">Hortative</a></i>
<ul><li><i>Negative hortative</i></li></ul></li>
<li><i>Negative</i>
<ul><li><i>Future negative</i></li></ul></li></ul></li>
<li><i><b>Voice relations</b></i>
<ul><li><i>Active</i></li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Passive_voice" title="Passive voice">Passive</a></i></li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Reflexive_voice" class="mw-redirect" title="Reflexive voice">Reflexive</a></i></li>
<li><i>Reciprocal</i></li></ul></li>
<li><i><b>Aspect</b></i>
<ul><li><i>Imperfective</i></li>
<li><i>Inceptive</i></li>
<li><i>Repetitive</i></li>
<li><i>Continuative</i></li>
<li><i>Habitual</i></li>
<li><i>Inchoative</i></li>
<li><i>Perfective</i></li></ul></li></ul>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="The_verbal_prefix">The verbal prefix</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Keres_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: The verbal prefix"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>In Keres, the verbal prefix carries information from five different grammatical categories: <a href="/wiki/Argument_(linguistics)" title="Argument (linguistics)">argument role</a>, <a href="/wiki/Grammatical_mood" title="Grammatical mood">modality</a>, <a href="/wiki/Affirmation_and_negation" title="Affirmation and negation">polarity</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-:4_7-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:4-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> person and number. That is, a single Keresan verb prefix codes who initiated the action and how implicated that entity is (the subject/case), whom underwent the effects of the action (the direct object), the speaker's assessment of the action (the modality)<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> and whether it occurred or not (polarity). On the other hand, information about when the action took place (i.e. <a href="/wiki/Tense%E2%80%93aspect%E2%80%93mood" title="Tense–aspect–mood">tense</a>) is expressed elsewhere in a clause, mostly by adverbs.<sup id="cite_ref-:5_8-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:5-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Number">Number</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Keres_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Number"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<p>Keresan verbs distinguish three numbers: <a href="/wiki/Grammatical_number" title="Grammatical number">singular</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dual_(grammatical_number)" title="Dual (grammatical number)">dual</a> (two entities) and <a href="/wiki/Plural" title="Plural">plural</a> (more than two entities);  and four <a href="/wiki/Person_(grammar)" class="mw-redirect" title="Person (grammar)">persons</a>: <a href="/wiki/Grammatical_person" title="Grammatical person">first</a> (the speaker), second (the hearer), third (a known, definite or salient entity being talked about) and <a href="/wiki/Obviative" title="Obviative">fourth</a> (a non-salient, unknown or indefinite entity being talked about, also known as obviative) persons. The plural and dual forms are often marked by reduplication of part of the stem (<i><b>gu</b>kacha</i> ‘s/he saw it’ vs <i><b>guʼu</b>kacha</i> ‘the two of them saw it’).
</p>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Argument_role">Argument role</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Keres_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Argument role"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<p>Languages encode two main types of actions: those in which the main participant initiates an action that produces change in an object (e.g. <i>kick <u>a ball</u>, buy <u>a gift</u>, cook <u>a dish</u>, read <u>a book</u></i>);  and those in which the action produces no (perceived) change in the world or that have no object (<i>sneezing, breathing, growing, diving</i>, etc.).<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup>  Actions that take an object are encoded by <a href="/wiki/Transitive_verbs" class="mw-redirect" title="Transitive verbs">transitive verbs</a>, whereas those that take no object are expressed via <a href="/wiki/Intransitive_verb" title="Intransitive verb">intransitive verbs</a>.
</p>
<h6><span class="mw-headline" id="Intransitive_verbs">Intransitive verbs</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Keres_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Intransitive verbs"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h6>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/Indo-European_languages" title="Indo-European languages">Indo-European languages</a> like English, all intransitive verbs behave similarly (‘They sneeze/breathe/dive/think’/etc.). In Keresan, actions that take no object are conceptualized in two distinct ways depending on how the initiator of the action is implicated. More active-like intransitive verbs (e.g. ‘to sneeze’) are coded through one set of morphemes, whereas actions conceptualized as involving the initiator at a lesser degree (e.g. ‘to believe’) are coded using a separate set of prefixes.
</p>
<table class="wikitable">
<caption>Degrees of involvement of the initiator in Keres<sup id="cite_ref-:4_7-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:4-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>
</caption>
<tbody><tr>
<th>
</th>
<th>Actions
</th>
<th>Intransitive verb type
</th></tr>
<tr>
<td><b>More</b>
</td>
<td><i>to write</i> (-dyàatra), <i>to steal as a thief</i> (-chʼáwʼa), <i>to have diarrhea</i> (-ushchʼi),
<p><i>to leave</i> (-mi), <i>to whistle</i> (-srbiitsa), <i>to sweat</i> (-shdyuwàan’i)
</p>
</td>
<td>Active
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td><b>Less</b>
</td>
<td><i>to believe</i> (-hima), <i>to be born</i> (-dyá), <i>to sleep (</i>-bái),
<p><i>to be afraid</i> (-tyishu), <i>to forget</i> (-dyúmidruwi)
</p>
</td>
<td>Inactive
</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>Ideas expressed in Indo-European languages with adjectives are most often encoded by verbs in Keresan. That is, in Keresan one express the idea in the sentence ‘He is selfish’ by saying something along the lines of ‘He <i>selfishes</i>’. In such “actions”, the entity that is characterized by them is not implicated in the action directly (i.e. it's beyond their control), and thus belong in the Inactive intransitive category. The different sets of prefixes are shown below:
</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Aspect">Aspect</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Keres_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Aspect"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<h3><span id="Time_.28tense.29_adverbials"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Time_(tense)_adverbials">Time (tense) adverbials</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Keres_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Time (tense) adverbials"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The category of tense is expressed in Keresan via adverbs that indicate when the action about which one is speaking took place.
</p>
<table class="wikitable">
<caption>Time adverbials in Acoma Keres<sup id="cite_ref-:3_9-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:3-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>
</caption>
<tbody><tr>
<th colspan="2">Past
</th>
<th colspan="2">Future
</th></tr>
<tr>
<td>tsikʼínuma
</td>
<td><i>long ago</i>
</td>
<td>kúsra
</td>
<td><i>tonight</i>
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td>háma
</td>
<td><i>once, formerly</i>
</td>
<td>nacháma
</td>
<td><i>tomorrow</i>
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td>súwa
</td>
<td><i>yesterday</i>
</td>
<td>naháayashi
</td>
<td><i>day after tomorrow</i>
</td></tr></tbody></table>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Lexicon">Lexicon</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Keres_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Lexicon"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>New words are coined through a number of roots that are combined to pre-existing ones. Compounding is a common strategy for word building, although <a href="/wiki/Derivation_(linguistics)" class="mw-redirect" title="Derivation (linguistics)">derivation</a> also occurs.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Numerals">Numerals</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Keres_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Numerals"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The Keresan numeral system is a base 10 system. Numerals 11–19, as well as those between the multiple of tens, are formed by adding the word <i>kʼátsi</i> (/ kʼátsʰɪ /  'ten') <i>f</i>ollowed by the word <i>dzidra (</i>/tsɪtʂa/ 'more'). Numerals 20 and above are formed by adding a multiplicative adverb (<i>-wa</i> or <i>-ya</i>) to the base number and the word <i>kʼátsi</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-:4_7-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:4-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<table class="wikitable">
<caption>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Loanwords_from_Spanish">Loanwords from Spanish</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Keres_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Loanwords from Spanish"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/European_colonization_of_the_Americas" title="European colonization of the Americas">European colonizers</a> arriving in the <a href="/wiki/Southwestern_United_States" title="Southwestern United States">Southwest US</a> brought with them <a href="/wiki/Material_culture" title="Material culture">material culture</a> and concepts that were unknown to the peoples living in the area. Words for the new ideas introduced by Spaniards were often <a href="/wiki/Loanword" title="Loanword">borrowed</a> into Keres directly from <a href="/wiki/Early_Modern_Spanish" title="Early Modern Spanish">Early Modern Spanish</a>, and a large number of these persists in Modern Keresan.<sup id="cite_ref-:6_10-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:6-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<table class="wikitable">
<caption>

<th>Modern Spanish

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="In_popular_media">In popular media</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Keres_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: In popular media"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Keres was one of the seven languages sung in the Coca-Cola "It's Beautiful" commercial during the <a href="/wiki/Super_Bowl_XLVIII" title="Super Bowl XLVIII">2014 Super Bowl</a> featuring "<a href="/wiki/America_the_Beautiful" title="America the Beautiful">America the Beautiful</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1134653256">.mw-parser-output .side-box{margin:4px 0;box-sizing:border-box;border:1px solid #aaa;font-size:88%;line-height:1.25em;background-color:#f9f9f9;display:flow-root}.mw-parser-output .side-box-abovebelow,.mw-parser-output .side-box-text{padding:0.25em 0.9em}.mw-parser-output .side-box-image{padding:2px 0 2px 0.9em;text-align:center}.mw-parser-output .side-box-imageright{padding:2px 0.9em 2px 0;text-align:center}@media(min-width:500px){.mw-parser-output .side-box-flex{display:flex;align-items:center}.mw-parser-output .side-box-text{flex:1}}@media(min-width:720px){.mw-parser-output .side-box{width:238px}.mw-parser-output .side-box-right{clear:right;float:right;margin-left:1em}.mw-parser-output .side-box-left{margin-right:1em}}</style><div class="side-box side-box-right plainlinks sistersitebox"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1126788409">
